01/11/22, 17:45 - Chad: Terraform (Docker)
Open Docker and make sure it's running

Open main.tf file and make following changes
name = "nginx:latest"

ports {
    internal = 80
    external = 8000
}

Open cmd
Open directory of main.tf file using cd command
Run the following commands
Terraform init
Terraform plan
Terraform apply
Type yes and enter
Go to localhost:8000 on web browser
Terraform destroy
01/11/22, 17:45 - Chad: Terraform AWS 
1) under IAM
Create user
(Using access key) ID and click on create user
U will get access key ID and secret key ID

Then go to cmd type
aws configure
Then enter access key ID and secret key ID and region name

terraform init
terraform fmt
terraform validate
terraform apply
terraform show
terraform state list

Then change ami value 
(New value will be provided or idk)

terraform apply
terraform show
terraform destroy

22/02/23, 03:28 - Chad: identify the reasons to categorize digital evidences
Categorizing digital evidence is important for several reasons, including:

Organization: Categorizing digital evidence can help investigators to organize and manage large amounts of data. By grouping similar types of evidence together, investigators can more easily analyze and draw conclusions from the data.

Analysis: Categorizing digital evidence can make it easier to analyze the evidence and identify patterns or connections between different pieces of evidence. This can help investigators to build a stronger case and support their findings.

Presentation: Categorizing digital evidence can make it easier to present the evidence in court. By grouping similar types of evidence together, it is easier to present the evidence in a clear and logical manner that can be easily understood by the judge or jury.

Preservation: Categorizing digital evidence can help to preserve the integrity of the evidence. By identifying and categorizing different types of evidence, investigators can ensure that the evidence is properly preserved and that it can be used to support legal proceedings.

Prioritization: Categorizing digital evidence can help investigators to prioritize their analysis and focus on the most relevant pieces of evidence. By categorizing evidence by relevance, investigators can save time and resources by focusing on the most important pieces of evidence first.

Overall, categorizing digital evidence is an important step in the digital forensics process, as it helps investigators to manage, analyze, present, preserve, and prioritize evidence in a logical and efficient manner.

22/02/23, 07:43 - Chad: A partition is a logical section of a storage device, such as a hard drive, that is created to store and organize data. The creation of partitions allows for better organization and management of data, as well as the ability to install multiple operating systems on a single device.

Other terms related to file systems include:

File system: A file system is the way in which files are organized and stored on a storage device. It is responsible for managing the access to files, their allocation, and their security.

Format: Formatting is the process of preparing a storage device for use by creating a file system on it. This erases all data on the device and sets it up to be used with a specific operating system.

Cluster: A cluster is the smallest unit of storage on a storage device. It is made up of a fixed number of sectors and is used to allocate and manage disk space.

Directory: A directory, also known as a folder, is a container for files and other directories. It is used to organize and categorize files on a storage device.

File allocation table (FAT): FAT is a file system used on some storage devices, such as floppy disks and older hard drives. It uses a table to keep track of the location of files on the device.

NTFS: NTFS is a file system used on Windows-based computers. It provides improved security and reliability over previous file systems, such as FAT.

Inode: An inode is a data structure used in some file systems, such as Unix-based file systems, to store information about a file, such as its ownership, permissions, and location on the storage device.

22/02/23, 08:09 - Sanskar Bombil: There are several reasons why an investigation on volatile memory might be necessary or desirable. Some of these reasons include:

Digital Forensics: Volatile memory (such as RAM) can contain critical evidence in digital forensics investigations. This is because volatile memory is used by running processes and can contain data related to those processes, including login credentials, encryption keys, and other sensitive information.

Malware Analysis: Volatile memory can contain information about malware that is running on a system. By analyzing the contents of volatile memory, analysts can identify the behavior and capabilities of the malware and develop countermeasures.

Incident Response: During a security incident, volatile memory can be used to quickly identify the scope of the incident and determine which systems have been affected. This information can then be used to contain the incident and mitigate any damage.

Performance Analysis: Volatile memory is also important for system performance analysis. By monitoring the usage of memory, analysts can identify performance bottlenecks and optimize system performance.

Overall, an investigation of volatile memory is essential in many different contexts related to digital security, forensics, and performance analysis.

25/03/23, 12:57 - Swayam Chatur: public class Solution {
    public static int ArrayMinJumps(int[] arr) {
        int n = arr.length;
        int[] jumps = new int[n];
        if (n == 0 || arr[0] == 0) {
            return -1;
        }
        jumps[0] = 0;
        for (int i = 1; i < n; i++) {
            jumps[i] = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
            for (int j = 0; j < i; j++) {
                if (i <= j + arr[j] && jumps[j] != Integer.MAX_VALUE) {
                    jumps[i] = Math.min(jumps[i], jumps[j] + 1);
                    break;
                }
            }
        }
        return jumps[n-1] != Integer.MAX_VALUE ? jumps[n-1] : -1;
    }
}

31/03/23, 09:16 - Swayam Chatur: SSE (Sum of Squared Error): This is a measure of how far the data points are from their assigned centroids. It is calculated as the sum of the squared distances between each data point and its assigned centroid. The goal of a clustering algorithm is to minimize the SSE, which is equivalent to maximizing the similarity between data points within each cluster.

Absolute error: This is a measure of the absolute difference between the true values and predicted values of a clustering algorithm. It is calculated as the absolute difference between each data point and its assigned centroid. Like SSE, the goal of a clustering algorithm is to minimize the absolute error to maximize the similarity between data points within each cluster.

31/03/23, 20:23 - Swayam Chatur: The GSM (Global System for Mobile Communications) Radio Access Link provides security through a number of mechanisms, including authentication, encryption, and radio frequency (RF) channel hopping.

Authentication:

Authentication is the process by which the network verifies the identity of the user. This is achieved through the use of a Subscriber Identity Module (SIM) card, which contains a unique identification number for the user. When a user attempts to access the network, the network sends a challenge to the SIM card, which generates a response based on a secret key stored in the SIM. If the response matches the one expected by the network, the user is authenticated and allowed access.

Encryption:

Encryption is the process of encoding information in such a way that only authorized parties can access it. In GSM, encryption is used to protect the confidentiality of voice and data transmissions over the air interface. GSM uses a strong encryption algorithm known as A5, which is designed to prevent unauthorized access to user information.

Radio Frequency Channel Hopping:

RF channel hopping is a technique used in GSM to prevent interception of user information. The GSM system uses a number of radio channels to carry voice and data traffic. The system continually switches between these channels in a random pattern, making it difficult for an eavesdropper to listen in on a conversation or intercept data.

02/04/23, 20:43 - Sanskar Bombil: One of the employee of xyz company was suspected to stealing money electronically from the company account and depositing it into his own account, he is the new account manager and has been provided with personal computer with access to the internet he was always seen carrying a fancy flash drive he use on the computer to listen to mp3 music assume that investigation is completed write and analyse the investigation report. 
Investigation Report
Summary;
The investigation report describes an internal investigation conducted by the financial department of XYZ Company to determine the cause of unexplained losses in the company's account. The investigation identified the new account manager, Mr. John Smith, as a suspect in the electronic transfer of funds from the company's account to his personal account. A search warrant was obtained, and incriminating evidence was found, including a flash drive, a music folder on his computer, and bank statements showing large deposits in his personal account.
Based on the evidence collected, the report concludes that Mr. John Smith was indeed involved in the electronic transfer of funds. It recommends that the company terminates his employment, reports the matter to the police for further investigation and prosecution, and implements strict security measures to prevent similar incidents from happening in the future. The objectives of the investigation were to identify wrongdoing, determine Mr. John Smith's involvement, collect evidence, analyze the evidence, and provide recommendations to the company.

Objectives 
The objectives of the above investigation report are:
1.	To identify if there was any wrongdoing in the electronic transfer of funds from the company's account to an unknown account.
2.	To determine if the new account manager, Mr. John Smith, was involved in the electronic transfer of funds.
3.	To collect evidence to support or refute the suspicion of Mr. John Smith's involvement in the electronic transfer of funds.
4.	To analyze the collected evidence to arrive at a conclusion on whether Mr. John Smith was involved in the electronic transfer of funds.
5.	To provide recommendations to the company on the appropriate action to be taken, including terminating Mr. John Smith's employment, reporting the matter to the police, and implementing strict security measures to prevent future incidents.
  


Background:
XYZ company has been experiencing unexplained losses for the past three months. The company's financial department conducted an internal investigation and discovered that an electronic transfer of funds was made from the company's account into an unknown account. Further investigations revealed that the new account manager, Mr. John Smith, was seen carrying a fancy flash drive, and he had access to the company's computer with internet access.
Investigation:
We initiated an investigation to determine if Mr. John Smith was involved in the electronic transfer of funds. We obtained a search warrant to search his office and personal computer. During the search, we found several incriminating evidence, including a flash drive, a music folder on the computer, and bank statements showing deposits of large sums of money in his personal account.


Tools:

1.	Search warrant: A legal document that authorized the investigators to search Mr. John Smith's office and personal computer for evidence related to the suspected electronic transfer of funds.
2.	Computer forensic tools: Software tools used to acquire and analyze data from Mr. John Smith's personal computer, including the music folder, the flash drive, and any other files or data related to the suspected transfer of funds.
3.	Financial analysis tools: Tools and techniques used by the financial department to analyze bank statements and other financial data related to the suspected transfer of funds.
4.	Surveillance equipment: Equipment used to monitor Mr. John Smith's activities and movements within the company, which may have provided additional evidence or information related to the suspected transfer of funds.
It's important to note that the specific tools used during the investigation may vary depending on the circumstances of the case and the resources available to the investigators


Analysis:
Based on the evidence, we conclude that Mr. John Smith was indeed involved in the electronic transfer of funds from XYZ Company's account to his personal account. It is evident that he used the flash drive to store and transfer data, including the company's financial information. Furthermore, the music folder on his computer was a disguise for hiding the stolen data.
Conclusion:
Based on the investigation, we recommend that the company terminates the employment of Mr. John Smith and reports the matter to the police for further investigation and prosecution. We also advise the company to implement strict security measures, including monitoring employee access to the internet and the use of external devices such as flash drives. This will help prevent similar incidents from occurring in the future.
